    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_211042279" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/211042279" />
    <a title="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions"><img alt="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464118116p2/2602702.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/211042279?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" href="/user/show/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions">Christina (A Reader of Fictions)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375857676" href="/book/show/3233802-obernewtyn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions?shelf=series-not-finishing">series-not-finishing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer211042279" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5494603364934383641">First published in 1987, Obernewtyn really just reads like a book from that era. I don't really know how to explain that, except that I've read dystopian/post-apocalyptic fiction from then and from now, and it very much reads like the former. Partly, this stems from the formatting, broken into a number of short books, because in the 80s and 90s publishers did not have the same faith in teenage attention spans that they do now.<br/><br/>Pulled in by the pretty cover with the intense looking girl, pretty mo</span>
  <span id="freeText5494603364934383641" style="display:none">First published in 1987, Obernewtyn really just reads like a book from that era. I don't really know how to explain that, except that I've read dystopian/post-apocalyptic fiction from then and from now, and it very much reads like the former. Partly, this stems from the formatting, broken into a number of short books, because in the 80s and 90s publishers did not have the same faith in teenage attention spans that they do now.<br /><br />Pulled in by the pretty cover with the intense looking girl, pretty mountains and a cat, I had no conception of what I was getting myself into. Apparently, as the infodumping all over the beginning of the novel told me, humanity made machines that destroyed the world, irradiating and polluting it. Many people died immediately, but some hardy farmers survived. These farmers established a new order, one opposed to technology and worshipful of Lud (their God). They also dictated a policy to kill any seditious people and those affected by radiation, Misfits.<br /><br />Oddly, though, they don't kill ALL of the misfits. Some are kept alive as workers or sent to the mysterious estate of Obernewtyn, much feared, because, like with a roach motel, those who go there check in but don't check out. Elspeth, the heroine, has, of course, psychic powers, able to speak with animals in her mind and sometimes having prophetic dreams. She, as expected, gets discovered, though for the more minor misfit tendency of the dreams, and shipped off to Obernwtyn.<br /><br />There, mysterious happenings are afoot. People disappear. There's a creepy doctor running tests. A weird machine that attempts to take over Elspeth's mind. The people running Obernewtyn appear to be evil. On the other hand, for once in her life, Elspeth has real friends who know her for who and what she is and accept her. She has more freedom than ever before, but her life is in great danger.<br /><br />Obernewtyn failed to really shine, though the story does exhibit promise. For one thing, you never really learn anything about the characters particularly. While I liked Elspeth, Matthew and Dameon well enough, all I really know is that they're nice people with powers. The world building, too, is half-hearted. I enjoyed the idea of this book, but never got sucked into Carmody's world.<br /><br />Personally, I would label the book more post-apocalyptic than dystopian, though many people on Goodreads would disagree with me. There are elements of both, however. On the plus side, there's no romance in here, so I suspect there will be eventually. For now, it's a nice respite from the modern, romance-focused dystopian and post-apocalyptic tales.<br /><br />Despite how slow much of the book was for me, I am curious enough to keep going with this series, because, at the very least, the books are short. I suspect these might be more enjoyable for middle grade readers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5494603364934383641" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_119940949" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119940949" />
    <a title="Ksenia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/825809-ksenia"><img alt="Ksenia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388351518p2/825809.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119940949?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ksenia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ksenia" href="/user/show/825809-ksenia">Ksenia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375857676" href="/book/show/3233802-obernewtyn">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119940949" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12651763858453555208">So I got the first one from the library and towards the end of the first book I knew this was something interesting. But it wasn’t until the second book (at the end of the second book no less) when I knew I had something fascinating in my hands. The moment that really got me was when the horse Gahltha pledges his loyalty to Elspeth and promises to help her and never leave her side (there’s a reason why of course) but I was so moved by this previously-arrogant horse and his devotion, that my hear</span>
  <span id="freeText12651763858453555208" style="display:none">So I got the first one from the library and towards the end of the first book I knew this was something interesting. But it wasn’t until the second book (at the end of the second book no less) when I knew I had something fascinating in my hands. The moment that really got me was when the horse Gahltha pledges his loyalty to Elspeth and promises to help her and never leave her side (there’s a reason why of course) but I was so moved by this previously-arrogant horse and his devotion, that my heart melted right then and there. And then when I got to the third book, I was desperate to finish it and see what happens that one night I stayed up to finish Ashling without so much as speaking to my husband one night. And now I wait for the fourth book to come from the library. And to be honest, after finishing Ashling, I was left in a bit of a reading funk: I didn’t know what to read next. In a matter of a week, I picked up four books and didn’t finish any of them (although one I know I will return to shortly). I guess I went through some withdrawal and I hadn’t felt that since last year in the summer. So that wasn’t so much of a review as me wanting to gush about this series. Loving it! Oh, and to think this whole series was started when the author was still in high school??? The author has got quite the imagination and even though it takes place on Earth, it might as well be Middle-Earth or something else like it. It’s so wonderful to read the world she has created here. And the people as well…if you can, read them. Definitely do not give up on the first book: the books get so much more interesting and intricate, that you’ll be itching for the next book in the series, like I am.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12651763858453555208" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1232198219" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11295114085234731511">This is one of my all time favourite books - to lead into a series.. that is still being written 20+ years later!<br/><br/>It is another Dystopian-post apocalyptic style of fiction where after the 'Great White' has happened. We join the story of Elspeth several years later, there are 'Bad Lands' where 'White Stick' a source of energy is collected from by people who are 'misfits'.<br/>Basically a Nuclear war has occurred and the bad lands is where radiation still exists and the by-product is collected as a fuel</span>
  <span id="freeText11295114085234731511" style="display:none">This is one of my all time favourite books - to lead into a series.. that is still being written 20+ years later!<br /><br />It is another Dystopian-post apocalyptic style of fiction where after the 'Great White' has happened. We join the story of Elspeth several years later, there are 'Bad Lands' where 'White Stick' a source of energy is collected from by people who are 'misfits'.<br />Basically a Nuclear war has occurred and the bad lands is where radiation still exists and the by-product is collected as a fuel. The humans that are classed as misfits are people that are different, they either look different or have a power such as Elspeth who has the ability to read minds and communicate with animals. The humans that are sent to mine the white stick get sick and die, like radiation poisoning.<br /><br />Elspeth is young and is sent to a 'farm' for misfits, where she discovers there are others like her with their own powers.<br /><br />The books that follow Obernewtyn become very descriptive so I would suggest if you enjoy this first book continue with the rest, you will be well rewarded.</span>

<div id="review_2501354481" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2501354481" />
    <a title="Jaime K" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13180341-jaime-k"><img alt="Jaime K" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349381507p2/13180341.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2501354481?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaime K" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaime K" href="/user/show/13180341-jaime-k">Jaime K</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780312869588" href="/book/show/1961315.Obernewtyn">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2501354481" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer512770775688219211">"I dreamed your life has a purpose which must be fulfilled, for the sake of all things." - Sharna, Chapter XXV<br/><br/>This really sums up the importance of Elspeth Gordie throughout the course of this book.<br/><br/>There are a lot of 'typical' dystopian (before that was a genre) tropes, but I think that Carmody did this is a unique way, especially for 1987. <br/>Carmody has a great ability to describe an individual's emotions as another's feelings and scents. I wonder if she was empathic, as this articulation is fant</span>
  <span id="freeText512770775688219211" style="display:none">"I dreamed your life has a purpose which must be fulfilled, for the sake of all things." - Sharna, Chapter XXV<br /><br />This really sums up the importance of Elspeth Gordie throughout the course of this book.<br /><br />There are a lot of 'typical' dystopian (before that was a genre) tropes, but I think that Carmody did this is a unique way, especially for 1987. <br />Carmody has a great ability to describe an individual's emotions as another's feelings and scents. I wonder if she was empathic, as this articulation is fantastic.<br /><br />The Great White, a nuclear holocaust, occurred many years ago (the time frame is something I'm not sure of). After this, a Council of farmers took charge, which eventually led to an extreme religious order (the Herders), a fear of the unknown (various guises of empathic abilities), and a fear/desire to eliminate much of anything from the Beforetime. Mutants (those with abilities) are considered unsafe, burned at birth or later, if the abilities aren't realized until later in life. Or, they're allowed to live under essentially lock and key. They are deemed Misfits, whether they are actually a Misfit due to magic or because they're children of Seditioners. This latter group is of anyone who opposes the Council.<br /><br />Elspeth is sent to Obernewtyn, a northern castle (ahem, prison) with an unknown current master, an unseen Doctor and his "treatments," and secrets that bind the Beforetime to current time. <br /><br />I like that animals are able to pass on their memories.<br />The coachman, Enoch, is amazing. I hope my positive feelings about him are real.<br />Other orphan Misfits Matthew and Dameon are at Obernewtyn. I am wary of Matthew, and I hope my feelings about him are wrong.<br />A Druid, thought to be dead, is now a ghostly near-legend. Around Obernewtyn, he's even not considered to be dead.<br /><br />I just like this post-nuclear war world as it's believable and very interesting. I definitely want to continue the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="512770775688219211" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1955484952" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4934331591178836222">Have I said before how much I love audio books? They are the best way to read and do something else! So, with the long wait between titles, I've not wanted to get into <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13130788-the-red-queen' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <i>The Red Queen</i>
</a>, (<i>Obernewtyn</i> #7), because I've forgotten so much of the original story. Listening to Isobelle read her own work is magical, and despite how long ago it was written, <i>Obernewtyn</i> stands the test of time. Elspeth Gordie is the quintessential 'clueless' hero. Kept intentionally ignorant (an uneducated population is a </span>
  <span id="freeText4934331591178836222" style="display:none">Have I said before how much I love audio books? They are the best way to read and do something else! So, with the long wait between titles, I've not wanted to get into <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13130788-the-red-queen" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>The Red Queen</i>
</a>, (<i>Obernewtyn</i> #7), because I've forgotten so much of the original story. Listening to Isobelle read her own work is magical, and despite how long ago it was written, <i>Obernewtyn</i> stands the test of time. Elspeth Gordie is the quintessential 'clueless' hero. Kept intentionally ignorant (an uneducated population is a compliant population) the people of the Land are oppressed and fearful. Misfits are shunned, at the most extreme they are burned, and when Elspeth is outed as a Misfit she is sent to the mountains to live at Obernewtyn.<br />This is a story told within a complete 'world', which has been clearly and believably brought to life by Carmody, and the variety of characters and situations, although many, are deftly controlled to benefit the story. This was a most enjoyable reread, and I'm off to borrow the next in the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/49286-the-obernewtyn-chronicles" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Obernewtyn Chronicles</i>
</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47906.The_Farseekers" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>The Farseekers</i>
</a>.</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4UxyeapMKMn/obs/+zEit38OJ8//86XR6N9ITF9s3nFpd+qNXM1Rzd5A80S+w7eVBxVyQyMdVf8fbaBxFDsqdw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RT/ecMIMrIoPd0TrzRXeCiiPYYCFp9FTcVnWwmfis3TNBEaENI3Vji6WDJCI50soUJQ0DFlJIX2G6z7/LLVHcg==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/26878.Isobelle_Carmody">About Isobelle Carmody</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/26878.Isobelle_Carmody"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1253191710p3/26878.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/26878.Isobelle_Carmody">Isobelle Carmody
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8452595640604425514">Isobelle Carmody began the first novel of her highly acclaimed Obernewtyn Chronicles while she was still in high school. The series has established her at the forefront of fantasy writing in Australia.<br/><br/>In addition to her young-adult novels, such as the Obernewtyn Chronicles and Alyzon Whitestarr, Isobelle's published works include several middle-grade fantasies. Her still-unfinished Gateway Trilogy</span>
  <span id="freeText8452595640604425514" style="display:none">Isobelle Carmody began the first novel of her highly acclaimed Obernewtyn Chronicles while she was still in high school. The series has established her at the forefront of fantasy writing in Australia.<br /><br />In addition to her young-adult novels, such as the Obernewtyn Chronicles and Alyzon Whitestarr, Isobelle's published works include several middle-grade fantasies. Her still-unfinished Gateway Trilogy has been favorably compared to The Wizard of Oz and the Chronicles of Narnia. The Little Fur quartet is an eco-fantasy starring a half-elf, half-troll heroine and is fully illustrated by the author herself.<br /><br />Isobelle's most recent picture book, Magic Night, is a collaboration with illustrator Declan Lee. Originally published in Australia as The Wrong Thing, the book features an ordinary housecat who stumbles upon something otherworldly. Across all her writing, Isobelle shows a talent for balancing the mundane and the fantastic.<br /><br />Isobelle was the guest of honor at the 2007 Australian National Science Fiction Convention. She has received numerous honors for her writing, including multiple Aurealis Awards and Children's Book Council of Australia Awards.<br /><br />She currently divides her time between her home on the Great Ocean Road in Australia and her travels abroad with her partner and daughter. <br /><br /><i>Librarian's note: Penguin Australia is publishing the Obernewtyn Chronicles in six books, and The Stone Key is book five. In the United States and Canada this series is published by Random House in eight books; this Penguin Australia book is split into two parts and published as Wavesong (Book Five) and The Stone Key (Book Six).</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="8452595640604425514" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
</div>
